# Long-Term Development Direction Review

**Date:** 2026-07-08 18:28 local shell time (CST +0800)
**Scope:** current evidence-based review for LetheBot repair and long-term development. This replaces the archived review as an active planning document. Historical reviews in `docs/archive/**` remain context only and are not completion evidence.

## Executive Summary

LetheBot's product direction remains healthy: a local-first QQ / OneBot chatbot with a thick, governable memory layer, explainable context injection, Pi-based reasoning, audited tools, background workers, and user-controlled privacy/deletion.

The implementation is now healthier than the archived recovery review described: the current baseline gate is green, and major foundations for turn lifecycle, action execution, context traces, governed memory proposals, tool call persistence, durable job records, governance CLI inspection/lifecycle controls, operations metrics/readiness, local acceptance evidence capture/validation, and durable privacy preferences exist in the current dirty worktree.

However, the repository is not yet production-healthy:

- the worktree contains substantial uncommitted tracked and untracked changes;
- completion claims must still be tied to current command evidence and DB assertions;
- real SnowLuma/QQ soak remains manual/opt-in and was not proven by the latest deterministic gate, although fake deterministic private/group metadata acceptance, including CQ-string, segment-array metadata paths, CQ-string and segment-array media URL secret-metadata boundaries, sender display metadata redaction boundaries, unsupported notice/request/meta-event/message_sent/unknown-post-type, valid-JSON-but-non-object and malformed reverse HTTP payload, WebSocket valid-JSON-but-non-object, non-event object packet, and event/echo collision boundaries, unsupported message-subtype no-side-effect boundaries, malformed top-level message content boundaries, positive safe-integer numeric top-level ID fallback, segment-array non-positive/fractional numeric metadata-ID inertness, WebSocket supported private/group malformed top-level content, identifier, timestamp, media URL, malformed segment-array, and sender display-metadata boundaries, and outbound sent-message-id positive safe-integer numeric fallback, malformed structured response fallback, and HTTP/WebSocket top-level response data-container fallback evidence, HTTP/WS OneBot API-error diagnostic redaction, structured API-error diagnostic-container fallback, malformed top-level HTTP API response-container fallback, WebSocket API timeout cleanup, WebSocket close/stop/send-throw pending-request cleanup, and WebSocket lifecycle diagnostic redaction, plus a redaction-first evidence template, local validator, and redacted OneBot deploy/verify operator output now exist for controlled local runs, including embedded API-key-like token and numeric platform-ID-like detection;
- durable scheduler runtime integration now has an initial in-process `JobRepository`-backed poller for summary/extraction/retention/admin-digest/conflict/decay/consolidation, with deterministic evidence that final failure heartbeats keep redacted job linkage across later empty polls and clear after later successful work, returned worker completed-output diagnostics preserve adjacent secret/platform marker classes, unsupported durable job types fail terminally without retry churn, repository-level terminal failures skip retry scheduling while preserving redacted DB evidence, the opt-in local worker-soak command now exits non-zero for unhealthy aggregate results while preserving redacted JSON evidence, keeps stdout machine-readable JSON under default logging, and has spawned evidence for the documented no-`--db` temporary migrated SQLite path with aggregate-only rows and clean FKs, `ops:doctor` now gives read-only integrity/FK/schema/count/config-boolean preflight evidence without contacting OneBot or printing secrets, and `release:check` now names the deterministic install/update/release gate, but review handlers are still non-destructive and live soak remains unproven;
- CLI service methods and representative spawned command-parser paths are tested, including Commander-level parser error redaction, missing-option-value and empty-option-value redaction, help-path non-leakage/read-only evidence, `why` token-budget/action-decision suppressor display, context-trace durable metadata final-guard redaction, conversation-only validation, mixed turn/conversation - optional web UI and richer metrics/dashboarding remain future work.

## Current Evidence Baseline

Latest R0 rebaseline evidence is recorded in `docs/loop-state-recovery.md`.

Commands refreshed through 2026-07-08 18:28 local shell time (CST +0800):

```bash
git status --short
pnpm list @earendil-works/pi-agent-core @earendil-works/pi-ai --depth 0
pnpm typecheck
pnpm lint
pnpm test:run
git diff --check
```

Observed results:

- Latest Phase 5 acceptance DB summary exact group @bot required-hints slice strengthens `pnpm acceptance:db-summary -- --db=<path> --require-acceptance-hints`, a read-only aggregate helper mode for live acceptance DB evidence. It reports redacted-path integrity/FK status, private/group chat counts, per-path private/group flow counts, context trace counts, turn/action status counts, memory source/revision counts, tool/audit/failure counts, and boolean evidence hints while omitting row IDs, platform IDs, message text, memory content, tool payloads, audit details, and DB row contents. The required-hints mode exits non-zero unless integrity/FKs are clean and private and group paths separately have chat rows, context traces, completed turns, successful actions, a complete linked flow where the same completed turn has both a context trace and a successful action execution, and a source-linked complete reply flow where that turn uses its selected durable `context_pack_id` / `action_decision_id` rows, is tied to the same path's normalized chat row plus `chat.message.received` gateway QQ raw event, has a delivered reply action with `executed_message_id`, has that sent message persisted as a same-path `bot.response` / `bot-self` chat row, and proves targeted trigger evidence: private by `conversation_type="private"` and group by the triggering normalized chat row carrying `mentions_bot=1` for an exact bot mention, plus memory-governance rows. Targeted local acceptance evidence coverage passed with `34 passed`; `pnpm typecheck` and `pnpm lint` passed; final `pnpm release:check` exited `0` with `72 passed | 1 skipped` test files and `1141 passed | 8 skipped` tests. This reduces manual DB-evidence leakage and one-sided/empty/split/unlinked/selected-pointer-mismatched/non-QQ-raw-event/non-reply-success/missing-bot-response/ordinary-group-chat DB completion risk, but it does not supply the missing live SnowLuma/QQ evidence.
- Latest Phase 5 acceptance runtime-config exclusivity gate slice tightens `pnpm acceptance:validate-evidence -- <path> --require-complete` so completed evidence must select exactly one compose target, one Pi provider mode, and one OneBot transport. Missing or conflicting checked choices now produce exclusive-option findings. Targeted local acceptance evidence coverage passed with `24 passed`; final `pnpm release:check` exited `0` with `72 passed | 1 skipped` test files and `1131 passed | 8 skipped` tests. This prevents contradictory runtime configuration evidence, but it does not supply the missing live SnowLuma/QQ evidence.

## Long-Term Direction Map

### 1. Product Direction: Local-first Governable Memory Bot

Direction remains healthy. LetheBot should optimize for:

- user/group/conversation/system-scoped memory;
- inspect/approve/reject/disable/delete/restore/supersede flows;
- source metadata, revisions, audit logs, and rollback handles;
- privacy opt-outs such as proactive DM and memory association;
- `/why` or CLI-equivalent context trace;
- local storage by default.

### 2. Platform Direction: QQ / OneBot First

QQ through NapCat / SnowLuma / OneBot remains the first practical target. Multi-platform abstraction should not outrun the QQ path.

Healthy constraints:

- Gateway adapts protocol only.
- Ingestion writes raw events before derived rows.
- Platform IDs are operational identity data, not ordinary memory.
- Live acceptance is opt-in and must not leak secrets.

### 3. Architecture Direction: Modular Monolith with Hard Boundaries

The target remains a modular monolith with clear ownership boundaries:

```text
Gateway -> Ingestion -> Raw Event Store
                     -> Identity / Attention
Memory -> Context Orchestrator -> Pi Runtime -> Policy/Tools -> Action Executor -> Gateway
Workers -> Memory / Summaries / Governance
Governance CLI/UI -> Memory / Context / Audit / Jobs
```

The current implementation has moved toward this boundary model through repositories/services. Durable worker scheduling is now initially wired through `JobRepository` in the app runtime, but non-summary maintenance handlers and live soak evidence still need hardening.

### 4. Memory Direction: Thick Memory, Not Vector Store Only

Memory must remain a governed data model with scope, visibility, sensitivity, lifecycle, source links, revisions, audit, and deletion semantics.

Current healthy evidence:

- durable memory repository creates source/revision/audit evidence;
- proposal service and extraction worker enforce deterministic policy and privacy opt-outs;
- retrieval tests cover exclusion rules;
- governance CLI can inspect/control memory state.

Remaining direction:

- keep group-chat-to-user-memory conservative;
- improve conflict resolution/supersede automation beyond the current redacted conflict-detection audit path;
- keep secret/prohibited content out of ordinary prompts and durable memory.

### 5. Context Direction: Explicit Context Orchestration

ContextBuilder owns retrieval, filtering, ranking, token budgeting, prompt assembly, and trace evidence.

Current healthy evidence:

- context traces and selected/rejected memory evidence exist in tests;
- forbidden memory boundaries are covered by deterministic tests;
- CLI/governance paths can inspect trace evidence.

Remaining direction:

- improve participant context and actual token accounting over time;
- keep display names/group cards structured and untrusted;
- avoid raw account table injection.

### 6. Pi Runtime Direction: Reasoning, Not Storage/Execution

Pi should remain behind adapter/core interfaces. It may propose tool calls or actions, but durable mutation and platform delivery must pass through LetheBot governance services.

Current healthy evidence:

- Pi packages resolve;
- mock tests pass in the default deterministic suite;
- real API tests are skipped/gated when credentials are absent.
- the legacy DeepSeek e2e harness is now a deterministic guard instead of a fake live-provider suite; it does not read local secret files and no longer has placeholder real-API assertions.
- PiAdapter construction tests now prove custom `baseUrl` propagation for both DeepSeek-compatible and generic provider models, and the opt-in real-provider suite uses `PI_API_KEY` or `DEEPSEEK_API_KEY` with `baseUrl` rather than the ignored `baseURL` spelling.
- failed Pi turns now preserve observability without storing raw secret-like or
  QQ/platform-ID-like provider/runtime error text in `agent_turns.response_text`;
  both returned-failure and thrown-exception paths have DB-level e2e coverage.

Remaining direction:

- continue normalizing provider errors and timeouts;
- keep tool hooks policy-gated, audited, and redacted on both output and error paths.

### 7. Tools and Policy Direction

Tools must be registry-backed, policy-checked, sandboxed, audited, and secret-scanned. `evaluatorPolicy=bypass` only bypasses LLM review; it must not bypass deterministic L0 policy, permissions, sandboxing, or audit.

Current healthy evidence:

- action executor send-failure paths now redact secret-like and QQ/platform-ID-like
  error text before returning or persisting failed reply / `dm_user`
  executions; DB-level unit coverage and the app-level failed-action e2e path
  prove raw seeded API-key/token/platform values do not remain in
  `action_executions.error_message`.
- durable job/worker diagnostics now redact sensitive structured keys as well as
  values before persisting job/attempt results and worker heartbeat details.
- failed-turn error persistence now redacts secret-like and QQ/platform-ID-like
  Pi/runtime error text before durable storage while keeping hashes-only
  event-processing failure diagnostics.

Remaining direction:

- continue hardening dangerous tool evaluator linkage;
- keep output and error-path redaction tests strong;
- expand DB-level tool-call assertions when new tools are added.

### 8. Workers Direction

Workers should be durable, idempotent, observable, and source-linked.

Current healthy evidence:

- durable job repository, attempts, leases, and heartbeats exist;
- expired running job leases are now reclaimed with stale running attempts closed as failed before retry, failed attempts honor retry-delay `scheduled_at` before reclaim while other ready jobs can proceed, and type-filtered claim polling does not mutate unrelated expired max-attempt job types while still letting the matching typed poller record final failed job/attempt state, preserving attempt-level failure observability and FK-valid durable state.
- expired running jobs that already reached `max_attempts` are now cleaned up as failed during claim polling, with stale attempts closed, leases cleared, completion timestamps recorded, and FK-valid durable state.
- durable worker handler failures are redacted before returned task results and before `jobs.error`, `job_attempts.error`, and structured `worker_heartbeats.details` persistence, while max-attempt failure rows and heartbeat `current_job_id` linkage remain inspectable.
- durable worker completed outputs are redacted before returned task results and before `jobs.result` / `job_attempts.result` persistence, including object keys, adjacent secret/platform fragments with both marker classes preserved, and numeric platform-ID fields in structured diagnostics, preserving non-sensitive result fields and FK-valid completed state.
- operations metrics and governance inspection can read job state.
- operations metrics now include aggregate `jobAttempts.total`, `jobAttempts.byStatus`, and `workerHeartbeats.byWorkerType`, with unit and spawned ops CLI temp-DB coverage.
- spawned CLI inspection now proves max-attempt expired job cleanup is visible through `list-jobs`, `list-job-attempts`, and `summarize-governance-health`, with secret-like payload/idempotency redaction and FK-valid temp DB state.
- deterministic short scheduler soak now proves `WorkerScheduler` can drive `BackgroundWorker`/`JobRepository` across repeated ticks for summary, extraction retry, and later-scheduled retention jobs, with failed/completed attempt evidence, idle heartbeat cleanup, no stale running attempts, and FK-valid temp DB state.
- `pnpm ops:worker-soak` now provides an opt-in local synthetic timer soak on a migrated `/tmp` or explicit disposable SQLite DB, returning aggregate-only job/attempt/heartbeat/FK evidence while omitting payloads and error text; spawned ops CLI coverage proves completed jobs, planned retry evidence, idle heartbeat cleanup, clean FK state, and negative argument handling.

Current healthy evidence:

- the app runtime registers a durable background job processor, summary-discovery timer, retention-maintenance timer, admin-digest-maintenance timer, memory-conflict-maintenance timer, memory-decay-maintenance timer, and memory-consolidation-maintenance timer;
- summary, extraction, retention, admin-digest, conflict, decay, and consolidation jobs execute through `JobRepository` leases, attempts, and heartbeats;
- integration tests assert source-linked memory writes from a durable extraction job;
- integration tests assert admin-digest jobs write redacted system audit evidence without leaking seeded secret-like payload/error/tool values;
- integration tests assert conflict jobs detect active memory conflict pairs, write redacted memory audit evidence, and do not automatically mutate active memory state.
- integration tests assert decay jobs detect stale low-score active memory candidates, write redacted memory audit evidence, and do not automatically mutate memory lifecycle state, confidence, importance, or revisions.
- integration tests assert consolidation jobs detect duplicate active memory groups, write redacted memory audit evidence, and do not automatically merge/supersede/delete memory records.
- governance CLI can now explicitly approve a safe supersede from conflict or consolidation review audit evidence: records must be active, non-secret/non-prohibited, and share the same scope/owner/kind boundary; the old record is superseded with revision/audit details while the replacement remains active.
- spawned `why --turn` explainability now includes linked durable `tool_calls` summary evidence for the turn, reusing governance redaction and omitting tool input/output payloads while keeping action/context evidence read-only and FK-clean.
- governance CLI can list conflict/consolidation review audit candidates with memory-ID groups, redacted details, and resolved/unresolved status before approval.
- governance CLI can explicitly disable an active non-secret memory from `memory.decay.candidates_detected` review audit evidence, with revision/audit details and without changing confidence or importance scores.
- governance CLI can summarize conflict/consolidation/decay review queues by event type and resolved/unresolved status without exposing audit details, memory titles, or memory contents.
- governance CLI can summarize redacted operator health counts across review queues, actions, tools, jobs, worker heartbeats, and audit rows without exposing payloads or secret-like values.

Remaining gaps:

- conflict/consolidation workers remain detection/audit only and do not automatically mutate memory; broader merge tooling and richer review queues remain future work;
- decay worker remains review/audit only and does not mutate automatically; explicit governed disable approval exists, while score decay remains future work;
- consolidation handling is candidate/audit only; automatic merge behavior remains a future governed action path;
- live long-running worker soak has not been run in this checkpoint; current evidence is deterministic short-soak unit coverage plus an opt-in local synthetic timer soak command, not a real multi-hour runtime soak.

### 9. Governance and Operations Direction

CLI-first governance is the right current path. Web UI can come later after DB and CLI semantics are trustworthy.

Current healthy evidence:

- governance service tests cover memory, context/action/tool/job/audit/privacy surfaces;
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover invalid reviewed supersede/decay-disable approval paths without mutation, including missing audits, wrong review event types, mismatched memory references, and blocked sensitivity.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover memory lifecycle parser paths for `approve-memory`, `reject-memory`, `restore-memory`, `delete-memory`, `disable-memory`, and `enable-memory`, proving durable state transitions, memory revision/audit rows, failed-operation non-mutation, redacted secret-like missing IDs, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover memory lifecycle durable-audit summary/details redaction: a spawned `delete-memory` path with a seeded secret-like/platform-like memory ID proves durable `memory.create` and `memory.delete` audit summaries/details are redacted before persistence while raw `audit_log.event_id` remains the exact local lookup key and SQLite FKs stay clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover the `enable-memory` restore path with seeded secret-like/platform-like memory IDs, proving active-state restoration, `memory_revisions` `restore` evidence, durable `memory.restore` audit summary/details redaction, redacted operator output, exact raw local `event_id` lookup, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover `approve-memory` and `reject-memory` proposal paths with seeded secret-like/platform-like memory IDs, proving active/rejected transitions, `memory_revisions` `approve`/`reject` evidence, durable `memory.approve`/`memory.reject` audit summary/details redaction, redacted operator output, exact raw local `event_id` lookup, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover the ordinary `disable-memory` path with seeded secret-like/platform-like memory IDs, proving disabled-state transition, `memory_revisions` `disable` evidence, durable `memory.disable` audit summary/details redaction, redacted operator output, exact raw local `event_id` lookup, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover the explicit `restore-memory` path with seeded secret-like/platform-like memory IDs, proving active-state restoration from deleted records, `memory_revisions` `restore` evidence, durable `memory.restore` audit summary/details redaction, redacted operator output, exact raw local `event_id` lookup, and clean SQLite FK state.
- audit repository unit coverage now proves direct repository-backed audit writes, including `level='full'`, redact secret-like and QQ/platform-ID-like text from durable summaries and structured details before persistence, including nested JSON object keys/values and numeric platform-ID fields such as `senderId`, `group_ids`, and `messageId`, force the persisted `redacted` flag when redaction occurs, preserve raw local `event_id` filters, and keep SQLite FK checks clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover deterministic secret redaction across memory `list-memory`, `show-memory`, and `export-memory` paths using a legacy/direct SQLite row with source, revision, and audit evidence; `list-memory` human-readable ID/user/group/title/content output is redacted before printing, and missing `show-memory` errors redact secret-like/platform-ID-like IDs without changing JSON inspect/export contracts.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover invalid memory filter validation: invalid `list-memory` / `export-memory` `--state`, `--scope`, `--sensitivity`, and `--source-type` values fail with redacted concise stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no memory/source/revision/audit mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover representative invalid `--limit` validation for list/explainability commands: non-integer or out-of-range limits fail with redacted concise stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no governance/event/job/privacy mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover Commander-level parser error redaction: unknown commands, unknown options, and missing required arguments exit non-zero with empty stdout, redacted stderr, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no governance/event/job/privacy mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now strengthen explicit include-output redaction evidence: included audit details, action payloads/reasons, action execution audit entries, tool input/output, job payload/result/idempotency keys, job attempt results, and worker heartbeat details contain redaction markers, do not expose seeded secret-like values, do not mutate persisted rows, and keep SQLite FK state clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover boolean include-flag parser errors: extra values after `--include-details`, `--include-actions`, `--include-audit-entry`, `--include-payload`, and `--include-result` are rejected by Commander with redacted stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no persisted DB mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover extra positional argument parser errors for memory lifecycle, privacy opt-out, display-profile redaction, `why`, and `summarize-governance-health` commands: unexpected values are rejected by Commander with redacted stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no persisted DB mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover unknown-option parser errors for memory lifecycle, privacy opt-out, display-profile redaction, `why`, and `summarize-governance-health` commands: unknown options are rejected by Commander with redacted stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no persisted DB mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover missing required argument parser errors for memory lifecycle, privacy opt-out, and display-profile redaction commands: missing arguments are rejected by Commander with empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage from provided partial arguments, no persisted DB mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover missing option value parser errors for representative value options across memory inspection/export, `why`, audit/action/job/event-failure/privacy/display-profile/supersede commands: missing values are rejected by Commander before dispatch with empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage from already-provided sensitive arguments, no persisted DB mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover explicit empty option value parser errors for representative value options across memory inspection/export, `why`, audit/action/job/event-failure/privacy/display-profile/supersede commands: `--option=` values are rejected before business dispatch with empty stdout, Commander-style missing-argument stderr, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage from already-provided sensitive arguments, no persisted DB mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover group-scoped display-profile/nickname redaction: `redact-display-profile --group` preserves global and other-group rows, redacts only the targeted group rows, writes redacted system audit evidence, avoids display-name leakage, redacts QQ-like user IDs in the human-readable command result, and keeps SQLite FK checks clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover privacy-preference reason redaction, durable reason/audit-detail redaction, assignment-shaped user-filter display redaction, and type/state filtering: `set-privacy-opt-out` persists redacted reason text when operators paste secret-like or QQ/platform-ID-like values; `list-privacy-preferences` redacts secret-like opt-out reasons and QQ/platform-ID-like user fields, preserves both assignment-secret and platform markers for assignment-shaped canonical user IDs in display output, and still uses the raw canonical user ID for exact local `--user` filtering; filter variants avoid cross-returning another user/type/state; read-only list paths do not mutate privacy/audit/memory rows; and SQLite FK checks stay clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover invalid privacy-preference type/state validation: invalid `list-privacy-preferences --type`, `list-privacy-preferences --state`, `set-privacy-opt-out <preferenceType>`, and `clear-privacy-opt-out <preferenceType>` values fail with redacted concise stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no privacy/audit/memory mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover invalid memory-review filter validation for both inspection and summary commands: invalid `list-memory-reviews --status`, `list-memory-reviews --event-type`, `summarize-memory-reviews --event-type`, and `summarize-memory-reviews --status` values fail with redacted concise stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/stack/source-path leakage, no audit/memory/revision mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover `summarize-memory-reviews` filter variants for conflict review queues: event-type, memory, and unresolved-status filters return count-only matching review evidence, avoid cross-returning consolidation/decay distractors, omit seeded secret-like review details, do not mutate memory state/revisions or write lifecycle audit rows, and keep SQLite FK checks clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover representative audit/action/tool/job/worker filter variants and audit classification display redaction: filtered inspection avoids cross-returning distractors, default output hides payload/details/result/audit fields, redacts visible secret-like fields, and keeps SQLite FK checks clean. Inspection output also redacts platform-like actor, worker, lease, action/tool turn, action-execution executed-message, job, job-attempt, and worker-heartbeat current-job identifiers while preserving raw filter keys for local owner/admin lookup.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover invalid audit filter validation: invalid `list-audit --category`, `list-audit --level`, and `list-audit --risk` values fail with redacted concise stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no audit/memory/revision mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover invalid action/tool filter validation: invalid `list-action-decisions --decided-by`, `list-action-decisions --risk`, `list-action-executions --action-type`, `list-action-executions --status`, and `list-tool-calls --status` values fail with redacted concise stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no raw-event/turn/action/tool/audit/memory mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover invalid job/attempt/worker-heartbeat status validation: invalid `list-jobs --status`, `list-job-attempts --status`, and `list-worker-heartbeats --status` values fail with redacted concise stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no job/attempt/heartbeat/audit/memory mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover the max-attempt expired lease cleanup visibility path: failed jobs and failed stale attempts are inspectable with redacted payload/idempotency output, governance health increments failed-job attention counts, and SQLite FK checks remain clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover invalid `why --type` validation: unsupported conversation type values fail with redacted concise stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no raw-event/chat/turn/context/audit/memory mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover `why --turn` stored context-trace output: selected/candidate/rejected trace evidence is visible, secret-like values in stored trace fields are redacted, raw message text and memory titles/content are not printed, and SQLite FK checks remain clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover default `why` latest-turn selection: the command resolves the latest agent turn by `agent_turns.started_at`, uses that stored context trace, avoids cross-returning older turn evidence, redacts secret-like trace fields, avoids raw message/memory-title leakage, and keeps SQLite FK checks clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover `why --turn` rebuilt-trace output when no stored context trace exists: selected/candidate memory IDs, filters, identity fields, and recent message IDs are visible; secret-like recent-message IDs are redacted; raw event payload, raw message text, memory titles, and memory content are not printed; and SQLite FK checks remain clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover `why` missing-turn/no-turn failure safety: failures exit non-zero with empty stdout, concise redacted stderr, no source paths or stack traces, no DB mutation, and clean SQLite FK checks.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover group-context `why --turn` stored trace output: conversation type and redacted group ID are visible, selected/candidate/rejected group trace evidence is visible, private-memory rejection evidence is visible without content leakage, secret-like group/trace values are redacted, raw group message text and stored memory titles are not printed, and SQLite FK checks remain clean.
- `/healthz` now exposes count-only event-processing observability (`pending` and `failures`) while deterministic integration tests assert that event IDs, sender IDs, display names, and raw error strings are not leaked in the health payload.
- `/readyz` now exposes compact readiness status with configurable `LETHEBOT_READINESS_PATH`; deterministic config/deploy/e2e coverage proves default/override propagation and verifies the healthy 200, adapter-degraded 503, and DB-degraded 503 readiness payloads omit adapter URLs, tokens, DB paths, raw errors, QQ-like platform IDs, private conversation IDs, and raw message text.
- event-processing failures are also durably recorded in `event_processing_failures` with internal IDs and hashed diagnostics only, and `pnpm cli list-event-failures` can inspect them without returning platform IDs, message text, display names, or raw error strings.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover `list-event-failures` filter variants: stage and raw-event filters return only matching hashed diagnostic rows, avoid cross-returning distractor failures, redact secret-like details, avoid raw event payload/platform identifier leakage, do not write audit rows, and keep SQLite FK checks clean.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover `list-event-failures` output identifier redaction: raw `--raw-event` and `--turn` filters remain exact lookup keys, while platform-like output/display `id`, `rawEventId`, and `turnId` values are redacted; tests assert no distractor/raw ID leakage, no DB mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- spawned governance CLI tests now cover invalid `list-event-failures --stage` validation: invalid stages fail with redacted concise stderr, empty stdout, no secret/platform-ID/source-path/stack leakage, no raw event/turn/failure/audit mutation, and clean SQLite FK state.
- event-processing failure retention is configurable through `LETHEBOT_EVENT_PROCESSING_FAILURE_RETENTION_DAYS` and `pnpm ops:retention -- --event-failure-days=<days>`, with temp-DB tests proving old rows are purged without FK violations.
- pino-based runtime structured logs now pass through a redaction hook before write, covering secret-like strings, QQ/platform-ID-like strings including legacy/free-text values embedded after non-alphanumeric separators, adjacent secret/platform fragments such as `sk-...-qq-...` and assignment-shaped adjacent fragments such as `api_key=sk-...-qq-...` with both marker classes preserved, numeric platform-ID fields, dynamic object keys, and Error message/name values while replacing Error stack details with `[REDACTED:stack]` and preserving ordinary counters and intervals;
- `deploy-napcat.ts` direct console output now uses display redaction for OneBot verification success/error text, deployment helper paths/details, validation issues, troubleshooting URLs, and final CLI result/error display;
- operations metrics include context/action/job/job-attempt/heartbeat/event-processing-failure fields, including worker heartbeat type counts; JSON aggregate keys are display-redacted for secret-like and platform-ID-like dynamic values, and Prometheus keeps unknown dynamic labels in the bounded `other` bucket;
- operations metrics now include `jobs.expiredRunningLeases`, with unit and spawned ops CLI temp-DB coverage proving expired running leases are visible as count-only operator evidence without exposing job payloads.
- `/metrics` now exposes the same count-only operations snapshot over HTTP, with configurable `LETHEBOT_METRICS_PATH`; deterministic integration coverage seeds a secret-bearing job payload, proves metrics counts and FK-clean state, and proves payload/token/worker values are not returned.
- `/metrics?format=prometheus` and `pnpm ops:metrics -- --format=prometheus` now expose the same count-only operations metrics as Prometheus text; dynamic DB values used as labels are bounded to known lifecycle/status/type allowlists and unknown values are bucketed as `other`, with tests proving platform-ID-like/secret-like seeded label values are not emitted. The ops CLI validates `--format` as `json` or `prometheus` and rejects invalid values instead of silently falling back to JSON.
- `pnpm ops:worker-soak` is documented as an opt-in local scheduler soak preflight; it defaults to a migrated `/tmp` SQLite DB and reports aggregate-only worker evidence, not payloads or secrets.
- governance health now includes `jobs.expiredRunningLeases` and `attention.expiredRunningLeases`, with service-level and spawned CLI temp-DB coverage proving stale lease attention counts are visible without leaking job payloads, worker IDs, or secret-like seeded values.
- spawned ops CLI tests now cover malformed/unsafe backup, metrics, retention, worker-soak, and restore invocations: failures produce non-zero exit, empty stdout, useful display-redacted stderr, no unintended DB mutation, restore overwrite refusal without `--overwrite`, and clean FK state. Invalid values containing secret-like or QQ/platform-ID-like text are redacted before stderr display. Unknown options, unexpected positional arguments, missing option values, and values supplied to boolean flags are rejected before operation dispatch.
- `pnpm verify:onebot` now has deterministic unit coverage for the WebSocket `get_login_info` path, including token query handling, echo matching, API error handling, and no token leakage in error logs.
- fake/controlled OneBot HTTP acceptance now has deterministic private, group, private/group quote/media, and private/group segment-array metadata reply lifecycle smokes asserting raw event, chat message, context trace, agent turn, action decision, action execution, bot response rows, and `PRAGMA foreign_key_check`; group coverage includes group card, sender role, exact bot mention, quote/media metadata from both CQ-string and segment-array inputs, normalized raw-event payload without raw CQ tags, group context/action execution, and outbound bot response evidence; private segment-array coverage includes reply/image/record/text segment normalization, durable quote/media flags, context/action execution, outbound response persistence, and FK checks; group segment-array non-target mention coverage proves non-bot `at` metadata is durable without triggering Pi/context/action/reply; group segment-array reply-to-bot coverage proves `reply` segments targeting same-conversation stored `bot-self` messages trigger the Pi/context/action reply path without `at` mentions; group segment-array non-bot quote coverage proves `reply` segments targeting same-conversation human messages remain silent while preserving quote metadata; group segment-array cross-group bot quote coverage proves `reply` segments targeting `bot-self` messages from other groups remain silent while preserving quote metadata; group segment-array plain-text bot-id near-miss coverage proves ordinary `text` segments containing the configured bot QQ ID do not replace exact `at` metadata; group segment-array at-all coverage proves `at` metadata for `all` does not replace exact configured bot-account mentions; group segment-array numeric bot-at coverage proves numeric `at.data.qq` values still trigger exact configured bot-account mentions; malformed top-level OneBot string identifiers containing secret-like/platform-like fragments now fall back to bounded local/unknown IDs instead of synthetic persisted platform IDs; malformed boolean, object, array, null, and empty segment identifiers are ignored instead of being persisted as synthetic platform IDs; malformed media `url` values preserve media presence while omitting polluted URL metadata; unknown segment-array types are ignored without metadata, Pi/context/action, or outbound side effects; malformed non-string `text.data.text` values are ignored instead of being stringified into normalized message text; malformed segment-array entries and non-object/array `data` containers are ignored or treated as empty data without event-processing failure or metadata side effects; unsupported CQ-string tags are ignored without metadata, Pi/context/action, or outbound side effects; CQ-string `at all` group-wide mentions remain silent without exact configured bot-account mention detection; CQ-string known tags with empty/malformed `at.qq` / `reply.id` params remain inert while media tags preserve media presence without polluted URL metadata; CQ-string HTML-entity escapes in text and media URL params are decoded into normalized durable content without changing exact mention-trigger boundaries.
- current adapter review found no deterministic inbound folded-forward/reaction metadata parsing/persistence beyond capability declarations, so those acceptance checks remain future work rather than fake coverage.
- controlled fake OneBot acceptance now covers both group and private quote/media metadata lifecycles through raw event normalization, chat message flags, context trace, action execution, outbound response persistence, and FK checks.
- local acceptance docs include token-safe `pnpm verify:onebot` usage, offline compose syntax preflight for both local acceptance stacks, and redacted evidence expectations for manual real QQ/SnowLuma checks.
- `pnpm acceptance:evidence-template` now generates a redaction-first local acceptance evidence checklist under stdout or an explicit `/tmp` path, covering health/metrics including JSON and Prometheus text snapshots, `verify:onebot`, worker soak, private/group lifecycle, DB/FK, and memory/privacy evidence while prohibiting secrets, tokens, cookies, QR codes, private QQ IDs, group IDs, and raw message text; spawned CLI tests prove secret-like environment values are not leaked and overwrite behavior is explicit.
- `pnpm acceptance:validate-evidence -- <path>` now provides a local offline share-safety check for filled acceptance evidence files. It reports only rule IDs, line numbers, and counts, exits non-zero for likely sensitive findings, handles pnpm's standalone `--` argument separator, and spawned CLI/package-script tests prove unsafe seeded tokens, QQ-like IDs, and raw message text are not echoed.
- `pnpm acceptance:validate-evidence -- <path> --require-complete` now provides an opt-in completion gate for filled manual SnowLuma/QQ evidence: empty share-safe templates remain valid under default validation but fail complete validation until core health, OneBot, private chat, group @bot, memory/privacy, FK, evidence-validator self-checks, and final accepted checklist evidence are checked; tests cover incomplete templates, completed redacted evidence, checked placeholder rejection, conflicting accepted/not-accepted decisions, spawned CLI output, and no raw secret/platform/message echo.
- Complete acceptance validation also rejects checked failed/degraded/not-ready status values, requiring healthy `/healthz`, ready `/readyz`, completed private/group turns, and successful private/group action executions before evidence can pass completion mode.
- Complete acceptance validation now also requires governed-memory/privacy evidence: an allowed answer affected by governed memory without cross-scope/private-in-group leakage, conservative source-linked group-derived user memory handling, lifecycle/sensitivity exclusion evidence, and redacted governance CLI inspection.
- Complete acceptance validation now also requires command-preflight evidence:
  both compose `config --quiet` checks, aggregate-only `pnpm ops:worker-soak`
  success, FK-clean acceptance DB evidence, and non-leaking required-command
  summaries.
- `pnpm acceptance:db-summary -- --db=<path> --require-acceptance-hints` now provides read-only
  aggregate-only acceptance DB evidence for live runs, with redacted displayed
  DB path and no row IDs, platform IDs, raw messages, memory content, tool
  payloads, audit details, or DB row contents. The required-hints mode exits
  non-zero for empty, incomplete, one-sided, split, unlinked, selected-pointer
  mismatched, non-QQ/non-chat-raw-event, non-reply-success, or
  missing-bot-response private/group acceptance DBs where context/action
  evidence is not linked through the completed turn's selected
  `context_pack_id` / `action_decision_id` rows, that completed flow is not
  source-linked to the same path's normalized chat row plus
  `chat.message.received` gateway QQ raw event, the success is not a delivered
  reply action with `executed_message_id`, or the sent message is not persisted
  as a same-path `bot.response` / `bot-self` chat row; complete validation
  requires recording this helper's successful required-hints evidence.
- Complete acceptance validation now also requires exactly one checked local
  configuration option for compose target, Pi provider mode, and OneBot
  transport, rejecting missing or conflicting runtime configuration evidence.
- Local acceptance evidence validation now rejects raw QQ/group/platform-like
  numbers even if a nearby `<redacted>` marker or redacted note appears on the
  same line; operators must redact the actual identifier, not annotate around
  it.
- Local acceptance evidence CLI output now redacts sensitive-looking file paths in validation JSON, template write JSON, overwrite errors, missing validate-file errors, and top-level errors. Operations docs now require neutral `/tmp` evidence filenames or `pnpm --silent` when package-script arguments might contain tokens, QQ IDs, group IDs, usernames, or other private identifiers because non-silent pnpm can echo raw script arguments before the script runs.
- `summarize-governance-health --compact` now provides aggregate-only operator triage over the existing detailed governance-health summary; spawned CLI tests seed sensitive raw/action/tool/job/heartbeat/event-failure/audit data and prove compact output omits dynamic aggregate keys, row classifiers, payloads, raw IDs, secrets, platform identifiers, and stored free-text while preserving FK-clean read-only behavior.
- A fresh 60-second local synthetic worker soak exited `0` with aggregate-only output: `success=true`, `ticks=57`, `processed=8`, all 7 durable job types completed, planned retry observed, lease extension observed, idle worker heartbeat with no current job, and `foreignKeyViolations=0`; this remains synthetic local evidence, not real SnowLuma/QQ or multi-hour production soak.
- backup/restore/retention docs/scripts exist, and `pnpm ops:rehearse-maintenance`
  now performs a disposable migrated-DB rehearsal of backup, restore, read-only
  doctor before/after retention, restored-copy retention, fixed table counts,
  and FK-clean aggregate evidence without contacting SnowLuma/QQ/OneBot or
  model providers.
- `pnpm ops:rehearse-rollback` now performs a disposable migrated-DB rehearsal
  of backup plus overwrite restore to the original DB path after a synthetic
  update, using aggregate counts and SHA-256 fingerprints to prove the rollback
  removed synthetic update rows and restored the pre-update state without
  printing row payloads or contacting SnowLuma/QQ/OneBot.
- `pnpm deploy:docker`, `pnpm deploy:systemd`, and `pnpm deploy:pm2` now
  generate reviewable deployment artifacts that reference runtime environment
  variables instead of embedding the operator's current OneBot token, bot QQ ID,
  or OneBot URL values.

Remaining direction:

- expand spawned CLI parser tests beyond representative happy paths;
- keep local/container acceptance docs synchronized with actual env vars;
- perform real SnowLuma/QQ controlled soak only when local session/secrets are available.

## Health Diagnosis

| Area | Direction Health | Current Implementation Health | Diagnosis |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| Product vision | 9/10 | 7/10 | Vision is focused; core governance foundations now exist, but live QQ soak is not proven. |
| Architecture boundaries | 8/10 | 7/10 | Boundaries are improving through services/repositories; runtime scheduler wiring exists for key jobs, while live soak remains incomplete. |
| Memory governance | 9/10 | 8/10 | Source/revision/audit/proposal/privacy paths are strong, memory lifecycle now redacts secret/platform-shaped operator metadata before durable revision reasons and audit summary/details persistence, and display-profile/history persistence redacts secret/platform-shaped UI metadata; conflict/consolidation review can drive explicit safe supersede, but richer merge queues and live soak remain. |
| Context orchestration | 8/10 | 7/10 | Trace and exclusions exist; prompt-rendered recent-message, memory, group-participant display/card/role, and identity token-budget evidence plus structured display-name/group-card prompt boundaries have improved, including assignment-shaped secret/platform marker preservation in ContextBuilder prompt-data token accounting, while rejected-candidate reasons/token accounting can still mature. |
| Pi integration | 8/10 | 7/10 | Dependency/import drift is currently resolved, failed-turn error persistence is redacted, display metadata is structured/redacted before prompt injection, and real provider tests remain gated and no longer include placeholder pass assertions or implicit local secret-file reads; `why` can now include redacted linked tool-call summaries for turn-level operator explanation. |
| Tool policy | 8/10 | 7/10 | Production tool-handler non-null assertion lint debt is now removed, and tool/action persistence redaction covers metadata-independent secret-like outputs, handler errors, generic audit-repository summary/detail final-guard redaction, action send-failure error persistence, Pi failed-turn error persistence, evaluator-required dangerous execute-path rejection evidence, write-file handler path-boundary escapes, network allowlist non-exfiltration before fetch, and network exception error redaction, network response body/header/status-text redaction, and read-file output content redaction, and list-directory entry name/path redaction, and write/delete-file success output/audit path redaction, and file-operation known error/success-audit path redaction; broader sandbox/permission coverage can still deepen. |
| Workers | 8/10 | 7/10 | Durable records, retry-delay and type-filtered claim cleanup scheduling evidence, initial runtime scheduling, deterministic short scheduler soak, unsupported durable job types fail visibly instead of being coerced into summary work, worker process/list diagnostics redact secret-like and platform-shaped output, and the opt-in local 15-second plus 60-second worker-soaks currently pass for summary/extraction/retention/admin-digest/conflict/decay/consolidation with aggregate lease-extension, planned-retry, idle-heartbeat, and FK-clean evidence; review handlers are non-destructive and real multi-hour/live soak evidence is still missing. |
| Governance CLI | 8/10 | 7/10 | Service coverage is broad, representative spawned parser tests now cover lifecycle commands, missing-argument parser failures, missing-option-value and empty-option-value parser failures, extra positional parser failures, unknown-option parser failures, boolean include-flag parser failures, human-readable memory/display-profile identifier redaction, generic audit-repository durable redaction, memory/display-profile durable-audit summary/details redaction, and spawned `supersede-memory` revision/audit redaction; review candidates can be listed before safe supersede, governance-health aggregate keys are spawned-tested for redaction, and compact governance-health triage is aggregate-only/read-only/FK-clean, while negative/variant coverage can still expand. |
| Operations | 7/10 | 7/10 | Docs/scripts/metrics/governance health, compact `/readyz` healthy/adapter-degraded/DB-degraded coverage, count-only JSON and Prometheus-text `/metrics` output, opt-in worker soak, read-only `ops:doctor` DB/config preflight, `release:check` deterministic install/update/release gate, display-redacted ops CLI errors, explicit ops CLI argument rejection, and redaction-first local acceptance evidence template/validator exist; no latest live SnowLuma/QQ soak evidence. |
| Documentation process | 7/10 | 6/10 | Current docs are better organized, but requested repair docs had path drift and must be kept current. |

**Overall:** direction is healthy; implementation is recoverable and currently green under deterministic gates with zero lint warnings after the latest R7/R4 explainability slice, but not yet production-complete.

## Required Development Strategy

1. Treat current worktree, command output, tests, and DB behavior as authoritative.
2. Do not use `docs/archive/**` as completion evidence.
3. Maintain `docs/loop-state-recovery.md` at phase boundaries with dates, commands, pass/fail, known gaps, and next step.
4. Keep changes small and reversible.
5. Do not commit unless explicitly allowed.
6. Prefer DB-level assertions over shallow HTTP/mock-only tests.
7. Continue from the next unproven gap, not from stale completion claims.

## Recommended Next Work

1. Keep active status docs current after each verified slice, especially `docs/loop-state-recovery.md` and this review.
2. Continue R8 controlled OneBot metadata acceptance only where the adapter exposes concrete deterministic fields; unsupported notice/request/meta-event payloads and unsupported message subtypes are currently no-side-effect acknowledged, and folded-forward/reaction inbound metadata remains future work until such fields exist.
3. Harden durable scheduler integration:
   - add governed lifecycle mutation only after review/action semantics are defined;
   - extend longer local/manual soak evidence for worker leases, retries, and failure modes;
   - keep DB assertions for jobs/attempts/heartbeats/source links.
4. Expand spawned governance CLI tests for additional negative and variant display-profile/privacy/audit/action/tool/job commands.
5. Continue ops/acceptance hardening with real SnowLuma/QQ acceptance remaining manual/opt-in, or expand spawned governance CLI negative/variant coverage while preserving DB/FK evidence.
